better ways to grill fish this summer\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EOr you can pick a fish that&#x2019;s built like a steak. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m talking firm-fleshed, flavorful, meaty ones like halibut and salmon that can handle heat, the smoke, and a flip or two. To prep a grill for hardy fish, start by cranking it as high as it will go. You want the grates very, very hot, so cover the grill as it heats up. &#xA0;Once the grill is hot, use a steel brush with a long handle and some elbow grease to completely clean the grates. &#xA0;Cover again for 2 to 3 more minutes to bring the grates back to that piping hot level. &#xA0;(If using a grill pan on the stove, follow the same process; just make sure the exhaust fan is on high and a window is open.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F10975-two-ways-to-perfect-a-fish-glaze?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E 2 ways to perfect a fish glaze\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F40d6a32577526e99ecec0f333ff0947dcd648b51.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: thirschfeld)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EEach fish steak you are planning to cook should weight about six ounces, be at least a solid inch thick, and kept very cold.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Remove the steaks from the refrigerator just before you are ready to grill and pat them dry.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13360-grilling-crab-is-easier-than-you-think?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E Grilling crab is easier than you think\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDampen a wad of paper towels with canola or grapeseed oil liberally. Grab the oiled towels with a pair of tongs, and rub them along the grates of the grill. Reduce the heat to medium high and place the fish on the grill, skin-side up (there may be no skin on your fish steaks, but I am referring to the side that used to have the skin on).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ffood52.com\u002Fblog\u002F13258-what-to-do-with-leftover-salmon?utm_source=yahoohealth&amp;utm_medium=referral&amp;utm_campaign=fiveminutefish\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat to do with leftover salmon\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAfter about 2 minutes, the lower half of the fish steak closest to the heat will start to turn opaque. That&#x2019;s when you know it&#x2019;s time to flip. Use a spatula (one that is wide and has a tapered edge) to gently loosen the underside of the fish steak from the grill and flip quickly. Cook for another 2 to 4 minutes, depending on the thickness of the fish. To test if the steak is done, gently use a spatula to pry open the middle contours of the fish. If they are opaque, you&#x2019;re good to go. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca Well, actually, they do.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F0e948a3fb6623b7c39a1f565a62e7afcc99bea73.jpg\" alt=\"The 7 Best Yogurts to Cheer You Up\" width=\"500\" height=\"366\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWouldn&#x2019;t it be great if mood-enhancers came not in expensive pills like Prozac, but in creamy, delicious dessert containers? Well, actually, they do.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Shutterstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWouldn&#x2019;t it be great if mood-enhancers came not in expensive pills like Prozac, but in creamy, delicious dessert containers? Well, actually, they do. A new study has found that probiotic-laced foods like yogurt can balance out your gut bacteria in a way that significantly improves the way you feel about your life. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThink of your gut bacteria as your own internal spin doctors, dictating whether your mood is going to be positive, or downbeat. Recent research&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fpubmed\u002F?term=steenbergen++probiotics+leiden\"\u003Epublished\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in the journal \u003Ci\u003EBrain, Behavior, and Immunity\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, researchers at Leiden University in The Netherlands recruited 40 healthy volunteers. Half of them were given a probiotic-laced supplement, the others a placebo. Over the next several months, they were asked about their feelings and their outlook on life. Within about four weeks, the group that was receiving the probiotics began to answer their surveys in ways that demonstrated fewer negative feelings and more positive ones! \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe key to this mood boost: Feeding your belly bugs with the right kind of yogurts&#x2014;those containing live, active cultures and not too much sugar (which promotes the growth of downer bugs). The editors of \u003Ci\u003EEat This, Not That! \u003C\u002Fi\u003Emagazine have identified some of the most effective mood boosters in the grocery store.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"501\" height=\"367\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w501\u002F78c851792a7996579cce03f85a4b5804e66a296a.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST GREEK\u003Cbr\u003EFage Total 2% Greek Yogurt\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EThere&#x2019;s a reason Fage is one of the most popular Greek yogurts out there. &#x201C;While it&#x2019;s not organic, Fage is one of the&#x2013;if not the&#x2013;best-tasting Greek yogurt available,&#x201D; says says Stephanie Middleberg, MS, RD, CDN. The brand is also impressively high in protein, packing in 20 grams per 7-ounce container, as much as any nutrition bar. Just make sure you side-step flavors like honey, which can pack a Snicker&#x2019;s bar worth of sugar.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"512\" height=\"375\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w512\u002F63433c9e4f33b14bc4f9b5751342431e8282fa40.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST ORGANIC \u003Cbr\u003EStonyfield Organic Nonfat Greek Yogurt&#x2014;Plain\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EBecause they are made with organic cow&#x2019;s milk, a container of Stonyfield Organic provides \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.plosone.org\u002Farticle\u002FAuthors\u002Finfo:doi\u002F10.1371\u002Fjournal.pone.0082429\"\u003Emore\u003C\u002Fa\u003E heart-healthy fatty acids than conventional yogurts. We suggest sticking with the plain variety on a daily basis, since it&#x2019;s low in sugar and calories, but if you&#x2019;re looking for a sweet morning treat, pick up their blueberry flavor. Though the sweet stuff slightly outweighs the protein, it&#x2019;s a perfectly acceptable once-in-a-while, probiotic-filled treat. For more tricks to reduce bloat, improve mood&#x2014;and uncover your abs&#x2014;tap for these \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.zerobelly.com\u002F14-ways-to-lose-your-belly-in-14-days\"\u003E14 Ways to Lose Your Belly in 14 Days\u003C\u002Fa\u003E!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"456\" height=\"334\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w456\u002F0d59298f616a12b949a3e5b0a0d5efcb7ed7ff8f.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST GRASS-FED\u003Cbr\u003EMaple Hill Creamery Greek Yogurt\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EMaple Hill Creamery&#x2019;s yogurts are made just two ingredients: grass-fed milk and live cultures&#x2014;and although you pay a premium for it, it&#x2019;s worth the few extra cents. &#x201C;Grass-fed yogurt contains more omega-3s and conjugated linoleic acids, both of which help prevent heart disease, inflammation, diabetes and various cancers,&#x201D; Middleberg says. Bonus: The blends are rich, creamy and taste fresh from the farm.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"512\" height=\"300\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w512\u002F8deb885444e9d7a1fdf38cb0140092148736c726.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBEST ALT-YOGURT\u003Cbr\u003EElli Quark \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EGerman for &#x201C;fresh curd,&#x201D; quark is a spoonable cheese that&#x2019;s a creamier version of your go-to yogurt&#x2014;and could be the next big thing in the daily aisle. To achieve the thick, indulgent texture, makers stir curd to stop it from hardening, and the result is a smooth dairy cream that&#x2019;s free of the tang typically associated with unflavored Greek yogurts. The relatively neutral flavor lends itself well to adding your favorite mix-ins. Plus, just like Greek yogurt, quark is filled with good-for-you probiotics and hunger-busting protein. (There&#x2019;s up to 17 grams in a 6-ounce container.) They both have about the same number of calories, too. Brain Chemistry Behind Just One Bite And How To Beat It","summary":"You and dark chocolate have a long-standing love affair.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F805ee198a6b7429fd12eedd1094aa251823b27d2.jpg\" alt=\"The Brain Chemistry Behind &#x201C;Just One Bite&#x201D; And How To Beat It\" width=\"540\" height=\"306\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Ffavorite-healthy-chocolate-bars\u002F\"\u003Edark chocolate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E have a long-standing love affair. You&#x2019;re seduced every night. You&#x2019;d like to be monogamous, but coconut ice cream calls you. So do vegan chocolate chip cookies and crusty bread with olive oil. Cognitively, you know you shouldn&#x2019;t be eating these foods, but once you&#x2019;ve had a bite, you&#x2019;re done. You&#x2019;re intoxicated.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.psychologytoday.com\u002Fbasics\u002Fdopamine\"\u003EDopamine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E floods the brain and you continue eating these foods until there&#x2019;s nothing left. Moderation doesn&#x2019;t exist in your world, even though you wish it did. You really wish it did. You want nothing more than to be in control of what you put into your mouth. Why does it feel like there&#x2019;s an invisible hand guiding you towards these temptations? Why does it always feel like you need&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003Eone more bite? \u003C\u002Fi\u003EWe did a little investigating here at \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\"\u003ECharlotte&#x2019;s Book\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E and asked Food Coach NYC, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Fauthor\u002Fdana_james\u002F\"\u003EDana James\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIt&#x2019;s All In The Chemistry (So Relax About Your Willpower)\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe answer lies in your brain chemistry: neurotransmitters and conditioning. It&#x2019;s not your willpower, so drop the self-flagellation. Instead, be aware that there are biochemical forces at play. The good news is that you have the power to transcend these.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou&#x2019;re not driven in search of a dopamine high like a strung-out junkie, nor are you one of Pavlov&#x2019;s dogs, conditioned to salivate at the ring of a bell. You&#x2019;re a human being with the ability to stop, observe and change behavior at any moment. Being aware of what you&#x2019;re up against is the first part of breaking the addiction.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Feel-Good Signal\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen you eat a sweet food, it immediately sends a signal to the brain to release dopamine, a pleasure neurotransmitter. Dopamine feels good. It gives a sense of relief. It&#x2019;s the same neurotransmitter that is released during sex, recreational drug use and flirtation. Who doesn&#x2019;t want a little dopamine hit? Unfortunately, the more you provoke dopamine with food, sex, or drugs, the more your body stops listening to it. The result: you need even more stimuli for the same high. More chocolate, more ice cream, and more bread. If you think dark chocolate and bread don&#x2019;t have sugar, you&#x2019;ve been tricked. One quarter of a 70% dark chocolate bar is sugar, and bread converts to sugar.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated :&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Fcharlottes-pages\u002Fmenu-luminous-skin\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EMaximize Your Menu For Glowing, Luminous Skin\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere&#x2019;s also a serotonin influence and an endorphin response, particularly if the food contains wheat or dairy. Eat both dairy and wheat together and you&#x2019;ll hijack your brain with so many stimuli&#xA0;you may as well be injecting yourself with Prozac and Wellbutrin, because that&#x2019;s exactly what they do&#x2014;recycle old serotonin and dopamine so you have more.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERe-Train Your Brain, Defeat Your Subconscious Reactions\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENinety-five percent of our actions are based on our subconscious. Our subconscious is defined by memorized behaviors, emotional reactions, attitudes and beliefs. If you&#x2019;ve trained your body to over-eat, binge or numb yourself with food, that&#x2019;s what it&#x2019;s going to do, even if 5% of the brain is telling it not to. This is why it feels like there&#x2019;s an invisible force driving you towards something you know you shouldn&#x2019;t be doing. This pattern can be broken.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.charlottesbook.com\u002Fcharlottes-pages\u002Freduce-bloat-fodmap-defined\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EA Recipe to Reduce Bloat, Not Weight: FODMAP Defined\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAbstain from your trigger foods for 21 days so you can rebalance your brain chemistry. If this sends fear running through your body, you&#x2019;re using food as a drug. Food should produce a neutral response in the body. Therefore, it&#x2019;s even more imperative that you abstain. If you get a little teary, you&#x2019;re using food to numb an emotion. It&#x2019;s OK; we all do it. But that emotion enslaves you and binds you to food. Use pen and paper to get out how you feel. Food isn&#x2019;t there to medicate. It&#x2019;s there to heal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003ENew Neural Pathways = New Habits\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMake a different choice from the day before. Repeat, and repeat, and repeat, until the new behavior has become ingrained into your subconscious (typically 21 days). Don&#x2019;t underestimate how challenging this will be. You&#x2019;ll hear voices that will tell you it&#x2019;s OK to have just one bite, that you&#x2019;ve had a tough day and that you deserve it. The brain does this because it has to create new brain cells and new neural pathways to create a new habit. This is work for the body, and it doesn&#x2019;t like it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut you&#x2019;re not a slave to your brain. You&#x2019;re in control and you can direct it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhat will your new habit be? What&#x2019;s going to keep you strong through the next 21 days?&#xA0;How will you feel when you break the addiction?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECommit to this now. Be free. Products May Be Contaminated With Salmonella\" width=\"540\" height=\"445\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe recall comes after the USDA received reports that a cluster of people in Minnesota and Wisconsin became sick between mid-April and late June after eating Barber products.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Barber Foods)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBarber Foods is recalling more than 1.7 million pounds of frozen, raw, stuffed chicken that may be contaminated with salmonella, according to a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.fsis.usda.gov\u002Fwps\u002Fportal\u002Ffsis\u002Ftopics\u002Frecalls-and-public-health-alerts\u002Frecall-case-archi\"\u003EU.S. Department of Agriculture&#x2019;s Food Safety and Inspection Services announcement\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe recall comes after the USDA received reports of people in Minnesota and Wisconsin who became sick between mid-April and late June after eating Barber products. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENearly 30 products are included in the recall, which may be labeled under the brands Barber Foods, Sysco, or Meijer. (A full list of the products, along with their case code \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.fsis.usda.gov\u002Fwps\u002Fpor\"\u003Ecan be found here\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis news comes after an original recall on July 2, in which the brand recalled more than 58,000 pounds of frozen, raw, stuffed chicken. The product in question was Barber Foods Premium Entrees Breaded-Boneless Raw Stuffed Chicken Breasts with Rib Meat Kiev with a use by\u002Fsell by date of April 28, 2016, May 20, 2016 and July 21, 2016.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETwo additional patients have been identified by the USDA since the original recall, prompting the new announcement.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe particular strain of salmonella that has infected people&#x2014;salmonella enteritidis&#x2014;can cause fever, abdominal cramps, and diarrhea that begins 12 to 72 hours after a person eats contaminated food, according to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Fnczved\u002Fdivisions\u002Fdfbmd\u002Fdiseases\u002Fsalmonella_enteritidis\u002F\"\u003ECenters for Disease Control and Prevention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It usually lasts four to seven days, and can make a person sick enough to require hospitalization. Elderly people, children, and those who are immune-compromised are especially at risk.\u003C\u002Fp\u003EFood safety specialist Benjamin Chapman, PhD, an associate professor at North Carolina State University who has studied how people handle raw, frozen, stuffed, breaded chicken products, tells Yahoo Health that they&#x2019;re especially risky when it comes to salmonella.&#xA0;\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhy? Because of the way they appear, people assume that they&#x2019;re already cooked&#x2014;and don&#x2019;t cook them fully as a result. &#x201C;We have a responsibility to tell people that they need to cook these products properly,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;I don&#x2019;t think we do a good job of it.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EHis research discovered that, despite properly labeling, only a small percentage of people actually use a thermometer to make sure their chicken is properly cooked, as recommended. Consequently, they&#x2019;re at risk of contracting salmonella from their meat. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EUnfortunately, freezing doesn&#x2019;t kill salmonella. The pathogen won&#x2019;t multiply when it&#x2019;s frozen, but will be preserved. So, when you take a frozen chicken product out of the freezer, it can still be contaminated.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EFood safety expert Mike Doyle, PhD, director of the Center for Food Safety at the University of Georgia, says that proper cooking (bringing the meat&#x2019;s temperature to 165 degrees) will kill off the salmonella, but the real risk is in cross-contamination.&#x201C;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EIf you thaw the chicken, the juices can contain salmonella,&#x201D; he tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;And if you thaw the chicken on a plate, cook it, and put the chicken on the same plate, it&#x2019;s been contaminated.&#x201D; Doyle also notes that you can get salmonella on your hands after handling the chicken, which can then be transferred to anything you touch.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003EThe USDA reports that some people who became sick had properly cooked the chicken and used a food thermometer to confirm that it was properly cooked. That&#x2019;s a sign that cross-contamination was an issue, says Doyle.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe USDA stresses that while the products seem to be cooked, they&#x2019;re actually raw and should be handled with care to avoid cross-contamination in the kitchen. That means washing your hands and any surfaces after handling them, and keeping the chicken away from other food that won&#x2019;t be cooked.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003EIf you have any of these products in your freezer, it&#x2019;s safest to just throw them out. &#x201C;I wouldn&#x2019;t handle it,&#x201D; says Chapman. &#x201C;Send it back, take it to the seller, or get rid of them.&#x201D;&#xA0;\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe organization also reports some people who became sick had properly cooked the chicken and used a food thermometer to confirm that it was properly cooked. So, if you have any of these products in your freezer, it&#x2019;s probably safest to just throw them Women More Susceptible To Secondhand Smoke Exposure Than Men?","summary":"New research published in the American Journal of Preventative Medicine has found a consistent link between secondhand smoke and the risk of stroke. Interestingly, women are more at risk.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fce216ce175dbf209e72d84ec34555b2f5c487a6d.jpg\" alt=\"Are Women More Susceptible To Secondhand Smoke Exposure Than Men?\" width=\"540\" height=\"365\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhen you breathe secondhand smoke, it&#x2019;s &#x201C;like you are smoking,&#x201D; according to &#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.surgeongeneral.gov\u002Flibrary\u002Freports\u002F50-years-of-progress\u002Fexec-summary.pdf\"\u003ESurgeon General\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;2.5 million people have died in the U.S. from secondhand smoke exposure since 1964.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe dangers of secondhand smoke have been studied for years, and research concludes the same thing: it&#x2019;s definitely bad for you.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENow, new research published in the American Journal of Preventative Medicine has found a consistent link between secondhand smoke and the risk of stroke. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe study, which analyzed data from more than 20,000 nonsmokers aged 45 and up, found that those who were exposed to secondhand smoke were 30 percent more likely to suffer a stroke within six years.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd, here&#x2019;s a noteworthy additional finding: Researchers discovered that study participants who were exposed to secondhand smoke were more likely to live with a smoker &#x2014; and be female.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile the study&#x2019;s authors tell Yahoo Health the finding could simply be due to sampling, psychologists say they&#x2019;re not shocked.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELicensed clinical psychologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Faliciaclarkpsyd.com\u002F\"\u003EAlicia Clark\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, PsyD, tells Yahoo Health that women can have difficulty speaking up when their needs are in conflict with those of someone they love, as is often the case when smokers and non-smokers live together. &#x201C;Women are nurturers by nature, and this tendency likely influences how women navigate conflict,&#x201D; she says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fare-former-smokers-safe-after-15-years-121685128937.html\"\u003EAre Former Smokers&#xA0;&#x201C;Safe&#x201D; After 15 Years?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAs a result, she says, a woman may be more likely to avoid the inevitable conflict that can come with raising an objection to her partner&#x2019;s smoking habit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAtlanta-based psychologist and relationship therapist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.dccatlanta.com\u002F\"\u003EJared DeFife\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, PhD, agrees, adding that the study may reflect a gender difference in how men and women handle assertion, boundaries, and limit setting in their relationships. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile DeFife tells Yahoo Health that it&#x2019;s important to set boundaries and ground rules in relationships &#x2014; especially when it comes to your own health &#x2014; he acknowledges that a partner&#x2019;s smoking habit can be a tricky problem to navigate: &#x201C;When you have a partner who smokes and you want them to stop, you can be in a real bind.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut it&#x2019;s worth speaking up. According to the 2014 \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.surgeongeneral.gov\u002Flibrary\u002Freports\u002F50-years-of-progress\u002Fexec-summary.pdf\"\u003ESurgeon General&#x2019;s Report\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 2.5 million people have died in the U.S. from secondhand smoke exposure since 1964. The Surgeon General also notes that, when you breathe secondhand smoke, it&#x2019;s &#x201C;like you are smoking.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAll secondhand smoke isn&#x2019;t created equal, and the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cancer.org\u002Fcancer\u002Fcancercauses\u002Ftobaccocancer\u002Fsecondhand-smoke\"\u003EAmerican Cancer Society\u003C\u002Fa\u003E breaks it into two categories: sidestream smoke (smoke from the lit end of a cigarette, pipe, or cigar) and mainstream smoke (smoke exhaled by a smoker). Sidestream smoke has higher concentrations of carcinogens, is more toxic than mainstream smoke, and has smaller particles that can make their way into your lungs and cells more easily &#x2014; and people who live with a smoker are repeatedly exposed to both.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fis-this-the-best-way-to-get-smokers-to-quit-118954738327.html\"\u003E Is This the Best Way to Get Smokers to Quit?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESecondhand smoke exposure doesn&#x2019;t just raise a person&#x2019;s risk of stroke. A report published in the journal \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcirc.ahajournals.org\u002Fcontent\u002F111\u002F20\u002F2684.full\"\u003ECirculation\u003C\u002Fa\u003Econcluded that the negative effects on the heart from exposure to secondhand smoke are nearly as bad as the effects on those who actually smoke.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPeople exposed to secondhand smoke may also be at risk of developing cancer. According to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cdc.gov\u002Ftobacco\u002Fdata_statistics\u002Ffact_sheets\u002Fsecondhand_smoke\u002Fgeneral_facts\u002F\"\u003ECenters for Disease Control and Prevention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, secondhand smoke exposure caused more than 7,300 lung cancer deaths each year between 2005 and 2009 among adult non-smokers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESecondhand smoke is also linked to marital issues: DeFife points to research that has found a partner&#x2019;s smoking habit is a &#x201C;significant predictor&#x201D; of later divorce. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELuckily, overall secondhand smoke exposure is on the decline. CDC data found that, during 2011 to 2012, only 25 percent of nonsmokers had measurable levels of the tobacco smoke biomarker cotinine in their blood, compared to 40 percent during 2007 to 2008.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDeFife says secondhand smoke may also be becoming less of an issue for younger women: &#x201C;Younger adults today appear to be less tolerant of dating, living with, or eventually marrying a partner who smokes.&#x201D; Those who actually are in a relationship with a smoker are more likely to relegate them to a smoking area outside, protecting their own health in the process, he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBottom line: If you live with a smoker and are exposed to secondhand smoke, you need to speak up. Your health depends on it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fyikes-new-study-shows-scary-effect-of-smoking-on-110748176917.html\"\u003EYIKES: New Study Shows Scary Effect Of Smoking On The Brain\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! the 23-Year-Old Whose Body Is Turning into Stone","summary":"Chanel White, age 23, is living with a rare chronic disease that slowly hardens her skin and organs.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F4938094f495f8b08a0653e10e6c0c6565e15da31.jpg\" alt=\"Meet the 23-Year-Old Whose Body Is Turning into Stone\" width=\"540\" height=\"718\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EChanel White, age 23, is living with a rare chronic disease that slowly hardens her skin and organs.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;(Photo courtesy Chanel White)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI was diagnosed with systemic scleroderma right after I turned 20, just a couple weeks after my honeymoon, in October 2011. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI had never heard of scleroderma before the doctor told me I had it. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.hopkinsscleroderma.org\u002Fscleroderma\u002F\"\u003EScleroderma\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is an autoimmune disease where the body produces too much collagen. It&#x2019;s as if someone is pumping concrete into your body.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn systemic scleroderma, the collagen not only builds up in your skin and your vascular system, but also your connective tissue, the framework of the human body. If you didn&#x2019;t have connective tissue, you would be like Gumby and you&#x2019;d just fall apart. If you have too much, like me, you basically turn into a living statue.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe disease is rare &#x2014; fewer than 500,000 Americans have it &#x2014; and there is no cure. You could live five months or you could live 20 years. But based on how fast I started showing symptoms, when I was diagnosed, I was told 10 years would be fortunate. That was three years ago.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn that time, I&#x2019;ve realized that something so extremely broken can still be so beautiful. I&#x2019;ve learned that there is joy in letting go of what you can&#x2019;t change, in letting go of what you believe your life was intended to be, and instead accepting and celebrating and revering all that it gives. I can&#x2019;t do any more that my body will let me do and I have to accept that. Once you do that, you can find the beauty in a body vandalized like this.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F10-things-id-like-people-to-know-about-living-122951065778.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Things I&#x2019;d Like People to Know About Living With a Chronic Illness\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA Day in My Life\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the media, you see stories of people who are doing all of these amazing things when they are sick, and honestly for me and many others it&#x2019;s not that way. There are lot of naps, a lot of doctor&#x2019;s appointments, a lot of medication taking, a lot of being too sick to do anything. I think people aren&#x2019;t as interested in that; it&#x2019;s boring, but it&#x2019;s the reality. Illness is not a glamorous existence, and it&#x2019;s important for people to know that.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhen I get up in the morning, there&#x2019;s just a lot of pain. There&#x2019;s always a fresh wave of pain when I wake up. It&#x2019;s just a realization that, yep, this is your body, this is what you&#x2019;re living. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMy day starts with a handful of pills, a bunch of liquid supplementation, and getting my tube feed started. I take 28 different medications a day, each multiple times a day. I am overproducing collagen in my digestive tract, and so essentially my esophagus, my stomach, and my bowels are stone. I can&#x2019;t swallow food, and my stomach doesn&#x2019;t empty. It&#x2019;s like trying to drop nutrients into a rock. Everything is paralyzed.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m hooked up to tube feeds for 14 to 15 hours a day. The nutrition runs through a pump into a port in my abdomen. My stomach can&#x2019;t handle too much at once, so it has to go into my stomach very, very slowly &#x2014; about two ounces every hour.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETypically, I have anywhere from one to three medical appointments a day. I have a port in my chest for chemotherapy infusions. I have iron infusions every five days. I can have up to 20 appointments a month. It&#x2019;s overwhelming. There&#x2019;s not a lot of time to yourself when you&#x2019;re sick.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELife isn&#x2019;t very glamorous. There&#x2019;s a lot of Netflix watching and napping and puking and feeling horrible. There&#x2019;s also lots of talking to friends on Facebook, and blogging when I feel well enough. I live in pajamas. I probably own more pajamas than I do clothes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOn social media, I will post pictures of me smiling and wearing makeup when I do get out of the house. I don&#x2019;t want people to misinterpret the illness. But I also want to capture the moments where I&#x2019;m enjoying myself, because they won&#x2019;t happen often. I think it&#x2019;s important to show that you can still enjoy life in a broken body, but it&#x2019;s also important to have people understand that this one picture of me smiling is not me, it&#x2019;s the face that I put on. Those are the rare occasions that I try to enjoy when I get them. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-things-i-want-teens-diagnosed-with-a-chronic-119457175518.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E7 Things I Want Teens Diagnosed with a Chronic Illness to Know\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA Sudden, Shocking Diagnosis\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI started having symptoms just before I was diagnosed. It was almost one of those overnight things where you look down and just stare, wondering &#x201C;what is happening to my body?&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMy hands would turn this horrible shade of violet purple, and they would go completely numb. I never thought much of it; I just thought my hands were cold. But I wasn&#x2019;t cold &#x2014; this was happening in a 70-degree room. After a few weeks of that, I started losing hair, I was tired all the time, and the tips of my fingers were starting to look kind of weird.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne day, I looked down and I thought I had burnt my finger cooking. It looked like I had just sat my finger on a hot grill. It was black and scabby, and horrendously painful. Every time I touched it was excruciating. It didn&#x2019;t go away and wasn&#x2019;t getting better, so I finally went to a doctor. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EHe took one look at me and told me, &#x201C;You have scleroderma.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETypically, a scleroderma diagnosis takes years. Many people are misdiagnosed with lupus or other autoimmune diseases. I walked in and literally didn&#x2019;t even have a chance to say hello before the doctor was like, &#x201C;You have this horrible disease.&#x201D; I didn&#x2019;t know what to do. He gave me pamphlets to read, tons of medication to pick up from the pharmacy, and a new way of life to start. I started chemotherapy pills and immune suppressants right away. Immediately after that appointment, it was a drastic life change.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMy fingers are tight and swollen; I can&#x2019;t straighten them. They get these sores &#x2014; that word really doesn&#x2019;t do them justice &#x2014; they&#x2019;re ulcerations, dead skin and tissue. It&#x2019;s because that concrete is not only harming my skin, but it&#x2019;s also crushing my vascular system. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EA lot of people when I first received the diagnosis thought it only affected my hands. They&#x2019;d ask, &#x201C;How are your hands doing?&#x201D; And I kept trying to explain to them, &#x201C;Yes, you can see that my hands are purple, you can see they have sores on them, but that&#x2019;s also happening to my organs.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBecoming My Own Casket\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESince my diagnosis, it has been a snowball of one problem after another. In December 2014, I was walking up the stairs to the mall and collapsed. I was wheeled out and rushed to the emergency room. My body had just stopped. I couldn&#x2019;t walk, I couldn&#x2019;t lift my head &#x2014; I was lying in a hospital bed with a machine breathing for me. I was basically awake for a month but couldn&#x2019;t do anything on my own.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI don&#x2019;t have much of an immune system, so I get sick very easily. I ended up with meningitis, C. diff (\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mayoclinic.org\u002Fdiseases-conditions\u002Fc-difficile\u002Fbasics\u002Fdefinition\u002Fcon-20029664\"\u003EClostridium difficile\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a bacterial infection), and spinal fluid in my brain. It was to the point where they basically told my family,&#xA0;&#x201C;Say your goodbyes.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI recovered, obviously, and went to rehabilitation. I learned how to walk again with all of these people who just had their hips redone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the past year, the disease has started attacking my respiratory muscles. My diaphragm functions at about 18 percent, so breathing has become a difficulty. I carry around oxygen because if I talk for a long period of time, or walk for too long, I don&#x2019;t have the capacity to get my diaphragm moving and expand my lungs. This disease truly damages every inch of you.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EStrong Support\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m grateful that my entire family lives nearby. My number one supporter is my husband of four years.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWe were high school sweethearts. I was a competitive gymnast and had a scholarship to be a vocal performance major. We were going to go to college together. We had goals. Then things changed, and he has been so adaptive and so supportive. Every hospital stay, he slept in that uncomfortable chair. I&#x2019;m in a hospital sometimes for thirty days.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F910a1647aa359f8b09d4875df0c50b8d074f42a2.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EChanel White with her husband, Noel White, who she calls her number one supporter. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Chelsey Shaw Photography)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI absolutely would not be able to face this battle without him. I&#x2019;m not going to lie and say I don&#x2019;t have breakdowns and I don&#x2019;t get upset that I&#x2019;m dying at the age of 23. There are times when I can&#x2019;t be strong; it&#x2019;s just not in my power at that moment. He is able to look at me and just say, &#x201C;It&#x2019;s okay.&#x201D; Not that it&#x2019;s going to be okay because we both know that it&#x2019;s not going to be okay. But it is okay where we are at. We are together and he&#x2019;s going to be there.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELearning to Let Go\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis illness has opened my eyes to the world. Before I became ill, I really didn&#x2019;t have that perspective that life can be over in an instant. I never really had any major tragedies growing up. I never saw a lot of deaths. I never saw a lot of illness. And now I&#x2019;m thrust into this world where there is constant death and constant illness. I&#x2019;ve watched friends die. I&#x2019;ve watched just people go through suffering that no human should ever have to endure. I realize now that life is such a fragile thing and it can shatter in an instant. Once it does, you won&#x2019;t be able to put it back together &#x2014; you just have to move on as a changed person. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI feel that I am a completely different individual since I became sick, like it opened this part of me that I just didn&#x2019;t know really existed. I&#x2019;m stronger, more resilient. I understand that I need to stop and take time to do the clich&#xE9;s, like smell the flowers, take the longer journey, and just enjoy the little things. Small victories are important. I am happy if I can have a bed. I am happy if I make it to the couch. I am happy if I am able to drink a small amount of Gatorade and not throw up.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EPeople might say that I learned not to take things for granted, but it&#x2019;s not like that. I don&#x2019;t think people are taking things for granted if they don&#x2019;t understand. I don&#x2019;t think someone is a bad person for eating a cheeseburger and not enjoying it. When you&#x2019;re sick, it&#x2019;s a different way of life. You learn to accept it. You learn that, wow, being able to eat a cheeseburger is really great. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s not about whether you take things for granted or not. It&#x2019;s about understanding and accepting the life that you have. And making it the best you can. And celebrating what it is.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EChanel White blogs at&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fthetubefedwife.blogspot.com\u002F\"\u003Ethetubefedwife.blogspot.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F6-phrases-people-facing-serious-illnesses-would-119951034923.html\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E6 Phrases People Facing Serious Illnesses Would Rather Hear You Say\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! 061b28a5daf602.png","type":"image\u002Fpng","width":240,"height":68,"size_type":"original","formats":{}}],"url":"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002FRfhZ_vfeQZqibFhe2dh_72MLauo","source_url":"http:\u002F\u002F41.media.tumblr.com\u002Fa4aa7e7ed15d940da0af447a91e79427\u002Ftumblr_inline_nr6l0qmPe71siw1k7_540.png"}],"highlight_color":"#000000","data_version":"1","title":"This Mathematician Says She Can Determine Whether Your Relationship Will Last","summary":"When I heard a mathematician had developed a formula for lasting love, the only thing I did is let out a src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F31a24f45968184ec1b3af538c6e25548863d8af0.jpg\" alt=\"This Mathematician Says She Can Determine Whether Your Relationship Will Last\" width=\"540\" height=\"700\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWill you be together forever?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo:&#xA0;Kate&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003EPowers)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI may love discussing relationships, but I have a serious aversion to math. Anything above simple algebra can break me out into stress sweats. So when I heard a mathematician had developed a formula for lasting love, the only thing I did is let out a groan. Eventually I took a look, and it&#x2019;s actually quite simple&#x2014;so easy, in fact, that even I could add it up.\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFirst, you&#x2019;ll need to rate your mood, both with and without your guy, and then your reaction to him, whether positive or negative. Then, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.businessinsider.com\u002Fmathematical-secret-to-lasting-relationships-2015-6\"\u003Eclick here\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for the formula and how to tally it all up.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002Fblogs\u002Fsmitten\u002F2015\u002F06\u002Fsigns-he-is-in-love-men-boyfriend?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E25 Unmistakable Signs He&#x2019;s in Love With You\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENow, for the science behind it. In an article published this week in Business Insider, Hannah Fry, a math whiz who works for at the UCL Centre for Advanced Spatial Analysis in London, breaks down happily ever after in this formula, developed by another mathematician based on research at \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002Fblogs\u002Fsmitten\u002F2014\u002F05\u002Fjohn-gottman-marriage-advice?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003EThe Gottman Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E: The longest-lasting couples felt they had more positive interactions than negative ones on a daily basis, while those with the least longevity generally feel their negative interactions are more common than happy ones.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFry explains, &#x201C;In relationships where both partners consider themselves as happy, bad behavior is dismissed as unusual. &#x2026; In negative relationships, however, the situation is reversed. Bad behavior is considered the norm.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002F2008\u002F09\u002F10-things-hes-thinking-when-youre-naked?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Things He&#x2019;s Thinking When You&#x2019;re Naked\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EShe continues, &#x201C;The most \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002Fblogs\u002Fsmitten\u002F2015\u002F01\u002F5-things-that-happen-when-your?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003Esuccessful relationships\u003C\u002Fa\u003E are the ones with a really low negativity threshold. In those relationships, couples allow each other to complain, and work together to constantly repair the tiny issues between them. In such a case, couples don&#x2019;t bottle up their feelings, and little things don&#x2019;t end up being blown completely out of proportion.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you tally up your own relationship, let me know what you think about the formula and its accuracy. If not, a simple inventory of your happiness versus unhappiness over time with your guy should be enough to know where you fall on the spectrum.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy Here&#x2019;s how to settle your stomach and still get the nutritional benefits \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Image from Thinkstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou already know that kale may be \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.menshealth.com\u002Fnutrition\u002Feasy-kale-recipes?cm_mmc=Yahoo-_-Kales_Gross_Side_Effects-_-Entry-_-Kale_Ultimate_Health_Food\"\u003EThe Ultimate Health Food\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It&#x2019;s rich in vitamins A and C, potassium, calcium, iron, and folate, as well as the eye-healthy carotenoids lutein and zeaxanthin. It contains the flavonol kaempferol, which a study by Baylor College of Medicine researchers found helps stop pancreatic cancer cells from growing.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s one of the best things you can put in your body. But for some people, it exits the body in a less-than-pleasing way.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike how? Well, you may remember an unfortunate news item from 2013&#x2019;s Fashion Week in New York, when several models had to be &#x201C;treated &#x2026; for diarrhea from eating too much kale,&#x201D; according to the \u003Ci\u003ENew York Times\u003C\u002Fi\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere&#x2019;s a simple reason for this superfood&#x2019;s supergross side effect: carbohydrates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EKale is loaded with insoluble fiber and a carb called raffinose, neither of which can be broken down during digestion, explains Linda Ann Lee, M.D., director of the Johns Hopkins Integrative Medicine and Digestive Center.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EInstead, they both pass straight through your GI tract to your colon, where bacteria begin converting them to acids, gases, and alcohols.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe end result of this fermentation process: You&#x2019;re perched on the porcelain throne.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.menshealth.com\u002Fnutrition\u002Fsnacks-you-can-actually-binge-eat?cm_mmc=Yahoo-_-Kales_Gross_Side_Effects-_-Entry-_-Foods_You_Can_Binge\"\u003E4 Foods You Can Actually Binge On\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnother reason might be the volume of kale you&#x2019;re eating, especially if you&#x2019;re a kale newbie. &#x201C;Suddenly eating huge amounts of any high fiber food may cause digestive disturbances,&#x201D; &#xA0;says Colleen Gerg, R.D., a dietitian based in Philadelphia.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s easy to get carried away with kale consumption, especially if you&#x2019;re juicing it. &#x201C;Because juicing greens requires very large amounts of the vegetable to create a glass of juice, you&#x2019;re getting very high concentrations of nutrients which your body may not be used to in such large amounts,&#x201D; she says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGerg suggests mixing up your ingredients by &#x201C;eating the rainbow.&#x201D; Balance out the kale with some reds (red bell peppers, tomatoes, raspberries); blues and purples (blueberries, red\u002Fpurple cabbage); and orange and yellows (summer squash, butternut squash, cantaloupe).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.menshealth.com\u002Fnutrition\u002Fhealthy-protein-smoothie-recipes?cm_mmc=Yahoo-_-Kales_Gross_Side_Effects-_-Entry-_-Protein_Packed_Smoothies\"\u003E20 Healthy, Protein-Packed Smoothie Recipes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGerg also recommends switching over to Tuscan kale, which has blue-green leaves and is less fibrous than red and curly Russian kale.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It has a slightly sweeter, more earthy flavor,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;Due to it&#x2019;s texture, it tends to be a bit more malleable and preferred when eating kale raw, as in salads.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYou may also need to cut back to about half an ounce a few times a week.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn your kale-free days, Gerg suggests swapping in other good-for-you greens, such as Swiss chard, spinach, collard greens, mustard greens, or dark green lettuces like arugula, romaine lettuce, mache, and spring mix. They contain the same prized vitamins and minerals as kale, but less fiber.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy the Editors of Men&#x2019;s So why do we always hold high expectations? \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Stocksy\u002FMarija Savic)&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.peacefulwarrior.com\u002F\"\u003EDan Millman\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is one of the stand-out authors, speakers, and spiritual giants in our world today. He has written over 16 books, given speeches all over the world, and has been a world-class athlete and coach for decades.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETalking with Dan was an incredible experience because he has so much perspective and such a calm energy that I could ask him anything and he had a wise answer.&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Flewishowes.com\u002Fpodcast\u002Fdan-millman\u002F\"\u003EWe talked about\u003C\u002Fa\u003E his journey to being a world champion in gymnastics, how he became a bestselling author, and his favorite books and spiritual leaders. But one of the most interesting things we talked about was how to alter your expectations in order to work with a clearer mind.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome people say that we should set really high expectations or else we won&#x2019;t have anything to work toward. Some say the secret of happiness is low expectations so we&#x2019;ll never be disappointed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut according to Dan, maybe it&#x2019;s best to have \u003Ci\u003Eno\u003C\u002Fi\u003E expectations. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMaybe we should recognize the truth: We have no control over the outcomes in our lives. We can only control our efforts. The truth is, we can do all the work, but &#xA0;if the timing is off or we&#x2019;re not in the right place at the right time, it&#x2019;s very possible that we still won&#x2019;t find the success we hope for.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf we can move away from worrying about fulfilling our expectations, we can make a good effort. And by making a good effort, we might get the outcomes we desire. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EKeeping an open mind will free you from worrying about meeting expectations you set for yourself. But don&#x2019;t think that this means we shouldn&#x2019;t make goals or have dreams &#x2014; we have to have a destination or motivation in mind in order to care about moving forward.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFind a goal you&#x2019;d like to move toward; put in the effort, and don&#x2019;t expect any specific outcome. Should You Shower  Morning or Night?","summary":"It seems like a simple question at first  are you better off showering before bed or when you wake up? But ask around and youll find your friends split into two very adamant camps.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fba54e5348a73995caacdef3df2dcec6242b26d4d.jpg\" alt=\"When Should You Shower &#x2014; Morning or Night?\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EPick a time, any time.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt seems like a simple question at first &#x2014; are you better off showering before bed or when you wake up? But ask around and you&#x2019;ll find your friends split into two very adamant camps. For night showerers, the idea of getting into bed covered in a day&#x2019;s worth of dirt and germs is downright repulsive. For the other team, starting your day covered in sweat from the night before &#x2014; and without the jolt of a morning shower &#x2014; is unfathomable. But which side is right?\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETurns out they both are, but it depends on the situation. Everything from your skin type to the amount of pollution in your life to when &#x2014; and how &#x2014; you work out can determine when you should shower.&#xA0;Here&#x2019;s how to find out which timing is best for you.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou should shower in the morning if&#x2026;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou have oily skin.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;&#x201C;Showering in the morning may help you perk up and can be especially good for those with oily skin, since oil can build up during the night and showers and excellent at clearing the pores,&#x201D; NYC-based internist \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fholly-phillips-md-internist-specializing-in-113433589918.html\"\u003EHolly Phillips, MD\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#xA0;tells Yahoo Health.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou like starting the day with a fresh shave.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;&#x201C;For men, showering can soften the hairs on the face, making shaving smoother and easier,&#x201D; Phillips&#xA0;explains.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou&#x2019;re OK with waking up early.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;One possible downside: the toll it takes on your beauty sleep. &#x201C;You may have to wake up earlier to bathe in the a.m. &#x2014; not ideal for those who like to hit the snooze button,&#x201D; says Phillips.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou&#x2019;re a night sweater.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;&#x201C;Obviously, if one is sweaty all night, they would want to shower in the morning,&#x201D; says L.A.-based dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.drkormeilidermatology.com\u002F\"\u003ETanya Kormeili, MD\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou&#x2019;re not around many germs.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;One of the biggest reasons to shower at night is to clean off the grime that accumulates over the day. If you bounce from home to car to air-conditioned office and back, you might not have much to scrub off. &#x201C;If you&#x2019;re covered up all day, just washing your hands and face and changing your clothes should do the trick,&#x201D; Phillip explains.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou should shower at night if&#x2026;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou need to chill out before turning in.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E &#x201C;Many find showering at night to be relaxing and a great way to unwind,&#x201D; Phillips explains. &#x201C;However, some research has suggested that showering at night may shift your body temperature in ways that can disrupt natural circadian rhythms, making falling asleep \u003Ci\u003Emore\u003C\u002Fi\u003E difficult. If this happens to you, try to shower a couple of hours before turning in.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou wear makeup. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#x201C;If you wear SPF or makeup, washing &#x2026; at night with a cleanser is super important,&#x201D; explains Kormeili. Washing your face without jumping in the shower may suffice, but the steam and constant flow from the showerhead could do a better job of cleaning off residue.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou have dry skin.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Use a morning shower as a time to deep-clean your less-than-dewy face? You might want to rethink it, Kormeili says. &#x201C;Washing in the morning with a cleanser is recommended only for oily patients, and not so much for patients who suffer from eczema or dry skin.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYour environment isn&#x2019;t exactly sterile.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Phillips says, &#x201C;As a resident, after working long shifts in the hospital around illnesses and germs, I would take off my clothes at the door and head straight to the shower to prevent bringing bacteria and viruses into the house.&#x201D; It&#x2019;s best to shower at night if you get particularly dirty over the course of your day &#x2014; either from a job (talking to you, construction workers) or environment (if you live in a polluted city, it&#x2019;s a good idea to wash off the grime). &#xA0;&#xA0;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYou work out (hard) during the day.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;&#x201C;If someone is very active or works outdoors during the day, they need a shower at night,&#x201D; Kormeili explains.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESo pick a morning or night shower depending on your body and lifestyle &#x2014; just make sure to avoid taking too many showers, Phillips warns. &#x201C;Overshowering (i.e., in the morning and at night) could wash away good bacteria that naturally protect the skin, or dry the skin out excessively, resulting in small cracks that can lead to skin infections.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:&#xA0;\u003Ca
